                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t col-right" style="max-width:500px;">
                     <div class="text-body-wrapper W-100 Font-B-1-160">
                      <noscript>
                      </noscript>
                      <div class="text-body W-100 Font-B-1-160" id="article-aft-text-body-104261960822" style="color:#222222;max-width:500px;">
                       <div class="body read-more-cut">
                        <div class="pre-cut" style="height:auto;margin-bottom:1.5em;">
                         <p>
                          <img alt="CDC Report: Fatal Overdoses From Prescription Painkillers Have Tripled" height="333" src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/2.0/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w500/994bc0ef0dffc35c6766ff13ec8dd91a52d6c771.jpg" width="500"/>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <em>
                           <strong>
                            Has our nations reliance on prescription painkillers gotten out of hand?
                           </strong>
                           (Stephen Lam/Corbis)
                          </em>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          The epidemic of opioid overdoses is continuing to take its deadly toll on Americans: The rate of deaths involving prescription painkillers like Oxycontin and Vicodin more than tripled between 1999 and 2012, according to a new
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:ec7c0bd6-7f98-3029-8855-c20006eb7d07;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://www.cdc.gov/nchs/data/hestat/drug_poisoning/drug_poisoning_deaths_1999-2012.pdf" target="_blank">
                           CDC report
                          </a>
                          . The heroin-related death rate is also on the rise, increasing nearly threefold in the same time period.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Despite these troublesome numbers, the CDC analysis did reveal one encouraging trend: From 2011 to 2012, the rate of prescription painkiller-related deaths dropped by 5 percent, marking the first such decrease in more than a decade.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          The rate of drug-poisoning deaths involving opioid analgesics is now starting to level off, Dr. Holly Hedegaard, a CDC epidemiologist who worked on the report, tells Yahoo Health. However, she cautions, this decline wasnt statistically significant. I wouldnt say this is the start of a downward trend  the death rate is just not increasing at the pace that it was between 2000 and 2006, when it was increasing about 18 percent per year, she says. What will it be like in 2013 or 2014? Theres no way I can project that.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <strong>
                           <em>
                            Related:
                            <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:ec7c0bd6-7f98-3029-8855-c20006eb7d07;t9:18;itc:0" href="https://www.yahoo.com/health/smoking-in-us-declines-to-all-time-low-104075451963.html" target="_blank">
                             Smoking in U.S. Declines to All-Time Low
                            </a>
                           </em>
                          </strong>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Dr. Andrew Kolodny, director of Physicians for Responsible Opioid Prescribing, takes a similarly conservative approach in interpreting the new data. I dont think theres anything to celebrate about until we see opioid overdose deaths in general coming down, he tells Yahoo Health. And that hasnt happened yet.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          The burgeoning opioid epidemic can be traced back to the late 1990s, when doctors began aggressively prescribing the drugs for chronic pain  a shift that Kolodny, also chief medical officer for Phoenix House, a nonprofit addiction treatment agency, blames on marketing campaigns launched by the makers of prescription painkillers.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          The message was that the compassionate way to treat complaints of pain  even common conditions like low-back pain, fibromyalgia, headache  was with an opioid prescription, Kolodny says. Doctors were told that these patients didnt face a high risk of addiction, since the maker of Oxycontin saw a fear of addiction as a barrier to sales, he says.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Consequently, as the rate of opioid prescriptions rose, there were parallel increases in addiction and overdose deaths.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Of course, not all of the nations overdoses occur in opioid addicts  the death rates include young people experimenting for the first time and patients with chronic pain who accidentally take too many pills. Those deaths are significant, Kolodny says. But the vast majority of deaths are occurring in people who are likely to be opioid-addicted.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          These arent necessarily the young pill poppers you might expect: The average painkiller overdose occurs in an adult between the ages of 45 to 54, says Kolodny. Its middle-aged folks, he says. This is a group that doesnt have to switch to heroin because theyre able to get pills from doctors. In fact, the increase in overdose deaths and medical visits for opioids has been greatest in the middle-aged and elderly population.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <em>
                           <strong>
                            Related:
                            <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:ec7c0bd6-7f98-3029-8855-c20006eb7d07;t9:18;itc:0" href="https://www.yahoo.com/health/the-sudden-death-of-18-year-old-logan-stiner-103108598762.html" target="_blank">
                             Overdosing on Caffeine: A Deadly Trend
                            </a>
                           </strong>
                          </em>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          However, he adds, I do think the medical community is beginning to recognize that we made a big mistake. So the medical community is beginning to prescribe more cautiously, which is what needs to happen to bring the epidemic under control.
                         </p>
                        </div>
                        <div class="post-cut W-100" id="post-cut" style="transition-property:none;-webkit-transition-property:none;transition-duration:10s;-webkit-transition-duration:10s;transition-timing-function:ease-in;-webkit-transition-timing-function:ease-in;overflow:hidden;max-height:0;max-width:500px;">
                         <p>
                          But even that isnt without its downside: As prescription painkillers become tougher to acquire, the shift to heroin may continue to accelerate.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Starting in the early 2000s, some painkiller addicts
                          <span>
                           
                          </span>
                          often those who used the drugs recreationally
                          <span>
                           
                          </span>
                          began switching to heroin (also an opioid), probably because it was easier to acquire. They have a harder time getting painkillers because theyre young and dont have any medical issues, Kolodny explains.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          That may explain why heroin overdoses typically occur in 20-somethings, who are actually dying at a much lower rate than the middle-aged and older folks who can get these pills directly from doctors, he says. One explanation: Heroin users typically take lower doses of the drug, compared to prescription pill users, since theyre unable to afford or acquire more. By contrast, the pain patients are getting massive, massive doses from doctors, Kolodny says. And they dont have to run around for it. Their insurance is paying for it.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          In 2012, there were about 6,000 overdoses involving heroin, compared to 16,000 involving prescription painkillers, according to the CDC report. Even so, heroin overdosing is a growing issue: Unlike the rate of deaths due to prescription painkillers, which recently declined, the heroin death rate leapt 35 percent from 2011 to 2012 alone.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Part of the problem: Young addicts are often afraid to seek medical attention for friends who overdose, reducing their odds of survival. They use with their peers frequently  theyll inject together, theyll buy drugs together, Kolodny says. When a peer has overdosed, people are afraid to call 911, because the police might come on the scene, and theyre worried theyll get arrested. Some states have passed Good Samaritan laws to circumvent this problem, yet the overdose rate is still rising.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Similarly, efforts to curb prescription painkiller abuse  for example, creating abuse-deterrent capsules  dont seem to be as effective as hoped. Making pills harder to crush and snort doesnt make them less addictive, says Kolodny.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          And although the CDC has named ending opioid abuse a top priority, the Food and Drug Administration continues to approve new opioids and continues to let them be marketed for conditions where theyre not safe or effective, he says. There are states across the country struggling to do what they can, but theyre really not getting the support they need from the federal government.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <em>
                           <strong>
                            Your Next Read:
                            <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:ec7c0bd6-7f98-3029-8855-c20006eb7d07;t9:18;itc:0" href="https://www.yahoo.com/health/vape-is-the-word-of-the-year-heres-why-thats-a-bad-103146763552.html" target="_blank">
                             'Vape' Is the Word of the Year. Here's Why That's a Bad Thing.
                            </a>
                           </strong>
                          </em>
                         </p>
                        </div>

                        <span class="item-title Font-A-3-120 D-b" style="word-wrap:break-word;margin-left:175px;">
                         One of the Best Things You Can Do for Someone With a Severe Mental Illness
                        </span>
                       </a>
                       <div class="item-a9n Tt-u Pt-4 Font-C-1-115 Fw-n" style="margin-left:175px;">
                        <a class="a9n" data-action-outcome="" data-ylk="g:e114ab5e-42f4-3ba7-a925-564e1bdac863;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:also;ad:0;cpos:2;itc:0;t9:29;elm:itm;elmt:link;" href="http://themighty.com" style="color:#999;" target="_blank">
                         The Mighty

                       </div>

                     <div class="item Td-n Pos-r D-b Ov-h SlowTrans has-image" id="article-aft-image-link-104261960822-124091775412" style="padding:0 0 40px;">
                      <a data-action-outcome="open" data-routable-url="/health/1/do-women-regret-abortion-new-study-helps-end-124091775412.html" data-ylk="g:9c4a13a8-cc4b-3d3d-9300-0362da164304;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:also;ad:0;cpos:3;itc:0;t8:tileview;t9:21;elm:img;elmt:ct;" href="/health/do-women-regret-abortion-new-study-helps-end-124091775412.html" style="color:#000;">
                       <span class="item-image Pos-r Fl-start Mend-20 Ov-h" style="background-image:none;height:103.62857142857143px;width:155px;">

WomenRegret Abortions? NewStudy Helps End Debate","summary":"We find that the negative emotions experienced at the time of the abortion wane\u002Fdecrease significantly over 3 years afterwards. Notably, relief remains the most common emotion.","body":"\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F17c659b4aa495afafaad534d874ca2c03e96c795.jpg\" width=\"540\" height=\"360\" alt=\"Do Women&#xA0;&#x2018;Regret&#x2019; Abortions? New&#xA0;Study Helps End Debate\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cb\u003E&#x201C;We find that the negative emotions experienced at the time of the abortion wane\u002Fdecrease significantly over 3 years afterwards. Notably, relief remains the most common emotion.&#x201D; \u003C\u002Fb\u003E(Photo: Getty Images)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ENew research has found that \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fjournals.plos.org\u002Fplosone\u002Farticle?id=10.1371\u002Fjournal.pone.0128832\"\u003Emore than 95 percent of women\u003C\u002Fa\u003E who have received an abortion have no regret about it, feeling that their decision was the right thing for them. Researchers found no difference in mental health outcomes between women who had first-trimester abortions and late-term abortions.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.guttmacher.org\u002Fstatecenter\u002Fspibs\u002Fspib_MWPA.pdf\"\u003EThirty-five states\u003C\u002Fa\u003E currently require some for of \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.guttmacher.org\u002Fpubs\u002Fgpr\u002F10\u002F4\u002Fgpr100406.html\"\u003Emandatory counseling\u003C\u002Fa\u003E for a woman before an abortion can be performed, \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.guttmacher.org\u002Fstatecenter\u002Fspibs\u002Fspib_MWPA.pdf\"\u003Eseven\u003C\u002Fa\u003E of which require a woman be told of possible psychological responses to abortion, stressing negative emotional responses such as &#x201C;\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.psychologytoday.com\u002Fblog\u002Fsomatic-psychology\u002F201010\u002Fpost-abortion-stress-syndrome-pass-does-it-exist\"\u003Epostabortion traumatic stress disorder\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&#x201D;, a term adopted by pro-life supporters but has not been accepted by the American Psychological Association or the American Psychiatric Association, and is basically debunked by this study.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe study, commissioned by \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.ansirh.org\u002F\"\u003EAdvancing New Standards in Reproductive Health (ANSIRH)\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, a think-tank at the University of California, San Francisco, confirms thirty years of research explicitly pointing towards there being no adverse mental health effects from abortion.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;As we note in our 2013 paper on women&#x2019;s emotions one week after the abortion, we found that many women experience negative emotions (anger, sadness, guilt, regret), as well as positive emotions (relief, happiness), with relief predominating,&#x201D; \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fbixbycenter.ucsf.edu\u002Ffs\u002Fbios\u002Frocca-corinne.html\"\u003ECorinne Rocca\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, PhD, MPH, an epidemiologist at the University of California-San Francisco and part of the ANSIRH research team, tells Yahoo Health, noting that in the team&#x2019;s new research, &#x201C;we find that the negative emotions experienced at the time of the abortion wane\u002Fdecrease significantly over 3 years afterwards. Notably, relief remains the most common emotion.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIn 2011, the Academy of Medical Royal Colleges (AMRC) in London reviewed all studies about the emotional effects of abortion that had been published in English between 1990 and 2011; from this, they concluded that it is an unwanted pregnancy that increases a woman&#x2019;s risk of problems with her mental health. AMRC researchers also deduced that a woman with an unwanted pregnancy is as likely to have mental health problems from abortion as she is from giving birth.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Ci\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002Fi-set-her-free-what-one-woman-wants-lawmakers-118896673772.html\"\u003EWhat One Woman Wants Lawmakers to Know About Her Late-Term Abortion&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe AMRC team also found that the factors that do increase a woman&#x2019;s risk of mental health problems after abortion are pressure from a partner to terminate a pregnancy, negative attitudes about abortion, and negative attitudes about a woman&#x2019;s experience of abortion.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIn other words, the stigma around abortion is more dangerous to a woman&#x2019;s mental health than abortion itself.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe ANSIRH researchers came to a similar conclusion, finding that it was women who perceived abortion stigma in their community (as well as those who terminated a planned and wanted pregnancy after the discovery of fetal abnormalities) that experiences for negative emotions.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;There is definitely a perception in public discourse over abortion that later abortion is more emotionally difficult than abortion in the first trimester, which is when over 90 percent of abortions in the US are done,&#x201D; says Rocca. &#x201C;In fact, as we note in the paper, the possibility that women having later procedures might be more likely to regret their abortions was part of the Supreme Court&#x2019;s justification for upholding a 2007 law banning a later abortion procedure. Our findings do not support this conclusion at all. Instead, we found that the emotions felt by women having abortions near gestational limits and women having first-trimester procedures reported the same levels of emotions; both experienced declines in negative emotions over time; and &#x201C;decision rightness&#x201D; was high among both groups.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EMost dramatically, the ANSIRH team also found that the predicted probability that 99 percent of women will ultimately report that abortion was the right decision for them at all time points in a three-year span following having received an abortion. The researchers also reported that &#x201C;being in school and working at the time of the pregnancy was associated with far higher feelings of decision rightness.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003ERelated:\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002Fwomen-face-harder-path-to-abortion-as-states-118873862652.html\"\u003E Women Face Harder Path to Abortion as States Extend Waiting Period \u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe researchers also drew an important &#x2014; albeit nuanced &#x2014; conclusion about the often politicized conversation surrounding abortion and women&#x2019;s mental health, stating that, &#x201C;Certainly, experiencing feelings of guilt or regret in the short-term after an abortion is not a mental health problem; in fact, such emotions are a normal part of making a life decision that many women in this study found to be difficult.&#x201D; That is, it is critical to not misinterpret emotions that come with normal life experiences as being negative side effects of abortion. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E &#x201C;Abortion has become an increasingly politicized topic in the US,&#x201D; notes Rocca. &#x201C;Groups interested in making it harder for women to get abortions have used the mental health damage argument to forward legislation restricting access. I think part of the reason these arguments perpetuate and continue to shape public perception has been the lack of rigorously conducted research examining the topic&#x2026;.Our study was very unique in that we are following hundreds of women seeking abortions at 30 facilities across diverse parts of the US over years to prospectively assess emotional and mental health outcomes. And, our findings do not support claims that abortion causes harmful psychological problems.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERead This Next:&#xA0;\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002Fmedical-abortion-can-be-safer-and-easier-for-women-109298214527.html\"\u003EMedical Abortion Can Be Safer and Easier for Women &#x2014; So Why Follow Old Protocols?\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003ELet&#x2019;s keep in touch! of the Best Things You Can Do for Someone With a Severe Mental Illness","summary":"Having an episode of psychosis or mania is hard.","body":"\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002Fa45aae7fe1fefb3babca89d60e3d6262d28563c9.jpg\" alt=\"One of the Best Things You Can Do for Someone With a Severe Mental Illness\" width=\"540\" height=\"357\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EHaving an episode of psychosis or mania is hard. Trying to put the pieces of my life back together afterward is brutal. But the things society says to me every day chip away pieces of myself, even when I should be repairing the damage.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EOnce a psychotic episode is over and I can think rationally, the things I did and said while psychotic cause me great shame. Not only do I have to live with telling people I was Jesus, how the government was out to get me, that I was being filmed or recorded or any number of other delusions I may have during an episode, I also have to live with the day to day barrage of messages from the outside &#x2014; messages that tell me I&#x2019;m dangerous and that my illness is something to make light of, even make fun of. I have to live with that stigma.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated:\u003C\u002Fb\u003E \u003Cb\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fthemighty.com\u002F2014\u002F09\u002Fwhen-i-noticed-my-wife-crying-behind-her-sunglasses\u002F?utm_source=yahoo.com&amp;utm_medium=referral&amp;utm_campaign=yahoo_links&amp;utm_content=Wife_Crying_Behind_Sunglasses\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003EWhen I Noticed My Wife Crying Behind Her Sunglasses\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EI&#x2019;m not going to go into all of the jokes and memes people say on social media every day that chip away at my self-esteem, but I will say that even people who like to call themselves progressive, loving and accepting join in the &#x201C;fun.&#x201D; Even people who think they are sensitive to social situations and people who are marginalized toss out words like insane, nut-job, lunatic and pass around cartoons depicting a &#x201C;crazy&#x201D; lady with PMS.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EWhen I see those words written from people who claim to like or love me, all I feel from them is a lack of understanding and hate. Yes, I literally feel as if they are sending hate at those who live with mental illness, and at me. Everyone in my life knows that I have schizophrenia. Anyone that wants to know what schizophrenia is like can read my book, Pills, Poetry &amp; Prose: Life with Schizophrenia, read my blog or even more amazing, they can ask me.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated:\u003C\u002Fb\u003E \u003Cb\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fthemighty.com\u002F2015\u002F02\u002Fi-have-ocd-this-is-what-its-like-to-be-in-my-mind-for-3-minutes2?utm_source=yahoo.com&amp;utm_medium=referral&amp;utm_campaign=yahoo_links&amp;utm_content=I_Have_OCD\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003EI Have OCD. This Is What It&#x2019;s Like to Be in My Mind for 3 Minutes.\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIf someone were to ask me what having schizophrenia is like, I would tell them it can be like going to a place with your worst fears, and living those fears out for days, weeks and possibly months. Are you afraid of being tortured? You will believe you are about to be tortured. Are you afraid of going to jail? You will believe you are going to jail. And then sometimes during psychosis, you will even be afraid of things you didn&#x2019;t know you were afraid of. I can think of nothing more appropriate to call it than hell on earth. In the beginning psychosis is usually pleasant for me, but it always turns to terror over time, and that terror is total and complete.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ESo, if you ever wonder what you can do for someone with a severe mental illness, I have a suggestion: You can help build them up. The world is already constantly tossing self-esteem battering messages their way. You can be the change in their lives. You can help them see their talents. You can help them see their strengths. You can point out their positives. You can be kind to them, because it is tough. It is so damn tough, and we all get tired. It&#x2019;s exhausting to constantly tell yourself you&#x2019;re OK when the world says differently. It&#x2019;s almost impossible to fight the world on your own. Be an ally. Spread the love.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated:\u003C\u002Fb\u003E \u003Cb\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fthemighty.com\u002F2015\u002F05\u002F31-secrets-of-people-who-live-with-anxiety\u002F?utm_source=yahoo.com&amp;utm_medium=referral&amp;utm_campaign=yahoo_links&amp;utm_content=Secrets_Anxiety\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003E31 Secrets of People Who Live With Anxiety\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003Eby \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fthemighty.com\u002Fauthor\u002Frebecca-chamaa\u002F\"\u003ERebecca Chamaa\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EMore from The Mighty:\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fthemighty.com\u002F2014\u002F10\u002Fwhen-i-overheard-a-conversation-between-my-son-with-autism-and-his-brother?utm_source=yahoo.com&amp;utm_medium=referral&amp;utm_campaign=yahoo_links&amp;utm_content=Conversation_Between_Brothers\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003EWhen I Overheard a Conversation Between My Son With Autism and His Brother\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fthemighty.com\u002F2015\u002F03\u002Fi-let-my-4-year-old-with-autism-use-my-camera-heres-how-he-sees-the-world\u002F?utm_source=yahoo.com&amp;utm_medium=referral&amp;utm_campaign=yahoo_links&amp;utm_content=Autism_Camera\"\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003EI Let My 4-Year-Old With Autism Use My Camera. Here&#x2019;s How He Sees the World.\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca \u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EI&#x2019;m talking firm-fleshed, flavorful, meaty ones like halibut and salmon that can handle heat, the smoke, and a flip or two. To prep a grill for hardy fish, start by cranking it as high as it will go. You want the grates very, very hot, so cover the grill as it heats up. &#xA0;Once the grill is hot, use a steel brush with a long handle and some elbow grease to completely clean the grates. &#xA0;Cover again for 2 to 3 more minutes to bring the grates back to that piping hot level. &#xA0;(If using a grill pan on the stove, follow the same process; just make sure the exhaust fan is on high and a window is open.)\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated:\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Ffood52.com\u002Fblog\u002F10975-two-ways-to-perfect-a-fish-glaze?utm_source=yahoohealth&amp;utm_medium=referral&amp;utm_campaign=fiveminutefish\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003E 2 ways to perfect a fish glaze\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"540\" height=\"359\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F40d6a32577526e99ecec0f333ff0947dcd648b51.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E(Photo: thirschfeld)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EEach fish steak you are planning to cook should weight about six ounces, be at least a solid inch thick, and kept very cold.\u003C\u002Fb\u003E Remove the steaks from the refrigerator just before you are ready to grill and pat them dry.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated:\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Ffood52.com\u002Fblog\u002F13360-grilling-crab-is-easier-than-you-think?utm_source=yahoohealth&amp;utm_medium=referral&amp;utm_campaign=fiveminutefish\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003E Grilling crab is easier than you think\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EDampen a wad of paper towels with canola or grapeseed oil liberally. Grab the oiled towels with a pair of tongs, and rub them along the grates of the grill. Reduce the heat to medium high and place the fish on the grill, skin-side up (there may be no skin on your fish steaks, but I am referring to the side that used to have the skin on).\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Ffood52.com\u002Fblog\u002F13258-what-to-do-with-leftover-salmon?utm_source=yahoohealth&amp;utm_medium=referral&amp;utm_campaign=fiveminutefish\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003EWhat to do with leftover salmon\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAfter about 2 minutes, the lower half of the fish steak closest to the heat will start to turn opaque. That&#x2019;s when you know it&#x2019;s time to flip. Use a spatula (one that is wide and has a tapered edge) to gently loosen the underside of the fish steak from the grill and flip quickly. Cook for another 2 to 4 minutes, depending on the thickness of the fish. To test if the steak is done, gently use a spatula to pry open the middle contours of the fish. If they are opaque, you&#x2019;re good to go. &#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Ffood52.com\u002Fblog\u002F13257-escabeche-the-best-make-ahead-post-beach-dinner?utm_source=yahoohealth&amp;utm_medium=referral&amp;utm_campaign=fiveminutefish\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003EEscabeche: the best make-ahead post-beach dinner\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ETo serve, pair your grilled fish with one of the following simple sauces:\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"540\" height=\"360\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F09e2bcbb10e6cd7f17406533a203112ec60e91de.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E(Photo: Alpha Smoot)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EI have my biases, of course.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cul\u003E\n \u003Cli\u003ELoosen Em-i-lis&#x2019;s Mint-Pistachio Pesto with just a bit more olive oil than the recipe calls for, and it will make a piece of grilled halibut seem Mediterranean even though it doesn&#x2019;t swim there.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n \u003Cli\u003EThe ingredients in hardlikearmor&#x2019;s Green Harissa make a versatile topping.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n \u003Cli\u003EGenius Recipes Torrisi&#x2019;s Spicy Sauce stands up to a fish with strong flavor.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg James Ransom)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cul\u003E\n \u003Cli\u003EAnd the roasted red peppers in Jean Anderson&#x2019;s Sweet Red Pepper Paste (Massa de Piment&#xE3;o) by Genius Report: Fatal Overdoses From Prescription Painkillers Have Tripled","summary":"Has our nations reliance on prescription painkillers gotten out of hand?","body":"\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"CDC Report: Fatal Overdoses From Prescription Painkillers Have Tripled\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002F994bc0ef0dffc35c6766ff13ec8dd91a52d6c771.jpg\" width=\"500\" height=\"333\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cem\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EHas our nation&#x2019;s reliance on prescription painkillers gotten out of hand?&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E(Stephen Lam\u002FCorbis)\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThe epidemic of opioid overdoses is continuing to take its deadly toll on Americans: The rate of deaths involving prescription painkillers like Oxycontin and Vicodin more than tripled between 1999 and 2012, according to a new&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.cdc.gov\u002Fnchs\u002Fdata\u002Fhestat\u002Fdrug_poisoning\u002Fdrug_poisoning_deaths_1999-2012.pdf\"\u003ECDC report\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. The heroin-related death rate is also on the rise, increasing nearly threefold in the same time period.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EDespite these troublesome numbers, the CDC analysis did reveal one encouraging trend: From 2011 to 2012, the rate of prescription painkiller-related deaths dropped by 5 percent, marking the first such decrease in more than a decade.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;The rate of drug-poisoning deaths involving opioid analgesics is now starting to level off,&#x201D; Dr. Holly Hedegaard, a CDC epidemiologist who worked on the report, tells Yahoo Health. However, she cautions, this decline wasn&#x2019;t statistically significant. &#x201C;I wouldn&#x2019;t say this is the start of a downward trend &#x2014; the death rate is just not increasing at the pace that it was between 2000 and 2006, when it was increasing about 18 percent per year,&#x201D; she says. &#x201C;What will it be like in 2013 or 2014? There&#x2019;s no way I can project that.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E\u003Cem\u003ERelated:&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002Fsmoking-in-us-declines-to-all-time-low-104075451963.html\"\u003ESmoking in U.S. Declines to All-Time Low\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EDr. Andrew Kolodny, director of Physicians for Responsible Opioid Prescribing, takes a similarly conservative approach in interpreting the new data. &#x201C;I don&#x2019;t think there&#x2019;s anything to celebrate about until we see opioid overdose deaths in general coming down,&#x201D; he tells Yahoo Health. &#x201C;And that hasn&#x2019;t happened yet.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThe burgeoning opioid epidemic can be traced back to the late 1990s, when doctors began aggressively prescribing the drugs for chronic pain &#x2014; a shift that Kolodny, also chief medical officer for Phoenix House, a nonprofit addiction treatment agency, blames on marketing campaigns launched by the makers of prescription painkillers.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;The message was that the compassionate way to treat complaints of pain &#x2014; even common conditions like low-back pain, fibromyalgia, headache &#x2014; was with an opioid prescription,&#x201D; Kolodny says. Doctors were told that these patients didn&#x2019;t face a high risk of addiction, &#x201C;since the maker of Oxycontin saw a fear of addiction as a barrier to sales,&#x201D; he says.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EConsequently, as the rate of opioid prescriptions rose, there were parallel increases in addiction and overdose deaths.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EOf course, not all of the nation&#x2019;s overdoses occur in opioid addicts &#x2014; the death rates include young people experimenting for the first time and patients with chronic pain who accidentally take too many pills. &#x201C;Those deaths are significant,&#x201D; Kolodny says. &#x201C;But the vast majority of deaths are occurring in people who are likely to be opioid-addicted.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThese aren&#x2019;t necessarily the young pill poppers you might expect: The average painkiller overdose occurs in an adult between the ages of 45 to 54, says Kolodny. &#x201C;It&#x2019;s middle-aged folks,&#x201D; he says. &#x201C;This is a group that doesn&#x2019;t have to switch to heroin because they&#x2019;re able to get pills from doctors. In fact, the increase in overdose deaths and medical visits for opioids has been greatest in the middle-aged and elderly population.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cem\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003ERelated:&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002Fthe-sudden-death-of-18-year-old-logan-stiner-103108598762.html\"\u003EOverdosing on Caffeine: A Deadly Trend\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EHowever, he adds, &#x201C;I do think the medical community is beginning to recognize that we made a big mistake. So the medical community is beginning to prescribe more cautiously, which is what needs to happen to bring the epidemic under control.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EBut even that isn&#x2019;t without its downside: As prescription painkillers become tougher to acquire, the shift to heroin may continue to accelerate.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EStarting in the early 2000s, some painkiller addicts \u003Cspan\u003E&#x2014;\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E&#xA0;often those who used the drugs recreationally \u003Cspan\u003E&#x2014;\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E&#xA0;began switching to heroin (also an opioid), probably because it was easier to acquire. &#x201C;They have a harder time getting painkillers because they&#x2019;re young and don&#x2019;t have any medical issues,&#x201D; Kolodny explains.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThat may explain why heroin overdoses typically occur in 20-somethings, who are &#x201C;actually dying at a much lower rate than the middle-aged and older folks who can get these pills directly from doctors,&#x201D; he says. One explanation: Heroin users typically take lower doses of the drug, compared to prescription pill users, since they&#x2019;re unable to afford or acquire more. By contrast, &#x201C;the pain patients are getting massive, massive doses from doctors,&#x201D; Kolodny says. &#x201C;And they don&#x2019;t have to run around for it. Their insurance is paying for it.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EIn 2012, there were about 6,000 overdoses involving heroin, compared to 16,000 involving prescription painkillers, according to the CDC report. Even so, heroin overdosing is a growing issue: Unlike the rate of deaths due to prescription painkillers, which recently declined, the heroin death rate leapt 35 percent from 2011 to 2012 alone.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EPart of the problem: Young addicts are often afraid to seek medical attention for friends who overdose, reducing their odds of survival. &#x201C;They use with their peers frequently &#x2014; they&#x2019;ll inject together, they&#x2019;ll buy drugs together,&#x201D; Kolodny says. &#x201C;When a peer has overdosed, people are afraid to call 911, because the police might come on the scene, and they&#x2019;re worried they&#x2019;ll get arrested.&#x201D; Some states have passed Good Samaritan laws to circumvent this problem, yet the overdose rate is still rising.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003ESimilarly, efforts to curb prescription painkiller abuse &#x2014; for example, creating &#x201C;abuse-deterrent&#x201D; capsules &#x2014; don&#x2019;t seem to be as effective as hoped. &#x201C;Making pills harder to crush and snort doesn&#x2019;t make them less addictive,&#x201D; says Kolodny.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EAnd although the CDC has named ending opioid abuse a top priority, &#x201C;the Food and Drug Administration continues to approve new opioids and continues to let them be marketed for conditions where they&#x2019;re not safe or effective,&#x201D; he says. &#x201C;There are states across the country struggling to do what they can, but they&#x2019;re really not getting the support they need from the federal government.&#x201D;&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cem\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EYour Next Read:&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002Fvape-is-the-word-of-the-year-heres-why-thats-a-bad-103146763552.html\"\u003E&apos;Vape&apos; Is the Word of the Year. Here&apos;s Why That&apos;s a Bad
